After he has received the profession of purity, the monk who has received the profession of purity should not run, nor should he rush, jump, jump over partitions, jump over ditches, jump onto verandas, sit in the sky above,{{note:{index:184,id:UT22084-001-002-603}}} go beyond the boundary, climb a ladder two rungs at a time, climb a staircase two steps at a time, spill over onto a causeway,{{note:{index:185,id:UT22084-001-002-604}}} fall asleep, or sit in equipoise. To fall asleep or to sit in equipoise are censured for two reasons: because one suggests disrespect and the other absentmindedness.{{note:{index:186,id:UT22084-001-002-605}}}
{{milestone:{label:3.21,id:UT22084-001-002-606}}}“Then, when the saṅgha elders say, ‘Venerable ones, profess the purity of those who have not come.{{note:{index:187,id:UT22084-001-002-607}}} Let their profession be known,’ the monk who has received the profession of purity should sit before the monk seated in front and say, ‘Venerable, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite, for the monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness, at such and such a place. {{page:{number:40,id:UT22084-001-002-1883,folio:F.150.b}}} The monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness, at such and such a place, declares that he is pure of hindering qualities. He professes the purity of his restoration rite and professes his purity. Let his profession be known.’
{{milestone:{label:3.22,id:UT22084-001-002-608}}}“This should be repeated verbatim a second and third time.{{note:{index:188,id:UT22084-001-002-609}}}
{{milestone:{label:3.23,id:UT22084-001-002-610}}}“Alternatively, the monk who has received the profession of purity should stand at the fore of the most senior row among the saṅgha and say, ‘Venerable saṅgha, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite, for the monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness, at such and such a place. The monk named so-and-so, at such and such a place, declares that he is pure of hindering qualities. He professes the purity of his restoration rite and professes his purity. Let his profession be known.’
{{milestone:{label:3.24,id:UT22084-001-002-611}}}“They will be guilty of a breach if the monk receiving the profession of purity follows the rules of customary conduct but his profession is not accepted after being properly received.”
{{milestone:{label:3.25,id:UT22084-001-002-612}}}The venerable Upāli asked the Blessed Buddha, “Honorable One, if the monk who has received a profession of purity comes to an end and dies on that very place after receiving a profession of purity, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:3.26,id:UT22084-001-002-614}}}“Upāli, it has not been received and should be received again.” 
{{milestone:{label:3.27,id:UT22084-001-002-615}}}“If the monk who has received a profession of purity{{note:{index:189,id:UT22084-001-002-6151}}} makes an oath professing to be a householder, or makes an oath that he is a novice, a person who has undergone castration, a person labeled a paṇḍaka, someone who has violated a nun, a matricide, a patricide, someone who has killed an arhat, someone who has caused a schism in the saṅgha, someone who has maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, a tīrthika, a convert to a tīrthika order, {{page:{number:41,id:UT22084-001-002-1884,folio:F.151.a}}} someone living under false pretenses, someone outside the common living, or someone denied the common living, has the profession of purity been received or not?” 
{{milestone:{label:3.28,id:UT22084-001-002-616}}}“Upāli, it has not been received and should be received again.”{{note:{index:190,id:UT22084-001-002-617}}}
{{milestone:{label:3.29,id:UT22084-001-002-619}}}“Honorable One, if the monk who has received a profession of purity comes to an end and dies while on his way after receiving a profession of purity, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:3.30,id:UT22084-001-002-620}}}“Upāli, it has not been received and should be received again.” 
{{milestone:{label:3.31,id:UT22084-001-002-621}}}“If the monk who has received a profession of purity makes an oath professing he is a householder, or makes an oath that he is a novice, a person who has undergone castration, a person labeled a paṇḍaka, someone who has violated a nun, a matricide, a patricide, someone who has killed an arhat, someone who has caused a schism in the saṅgha, someone who has maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, a tīrthika, a convert to a tīrthika order, someone living under false pretenses, someone outside the common living, or someone denied the common living, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:3.32,id:UT22084-001-002-622}}}“Upāli, it has not been received and should be received again.”
{{milestone:{label:3.33,id:UT22084-001-002-623}}}“Honorable One, if the monk who has received a profession of purity receives a profession of purity and then comes to an end and dies while among the saṅgha, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:3.34,id:UT22084-001-002-624}}}“Upāli, it has been received and should not be received again.”{{note:{index:191,id:UT22084-001-002-625}}}
{{milestone:{label:3.35,id:UT22084-001-002-626}}}“[Honorable One,] if the monk who has received a profession of purity makes an oath professing he is a householder, or makes an oath that he is a novice, a person who has undergone castration, a person labeled a paṇḍaka, someone who has violated a nun, a matricide, a patricide, someone who has killed an arhat, someone who has caused a schism in the saṅgha, someone who has maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, a tīrthika, a convert to a tīrthika order, someone living under false pretenses, someone outside the common living, or someone denied the common living, {{page:{number:42,id:UT22084-001-002-1885,folio:F.151.b}}} has the profession of purity been received or not?” 
{{milestone:{label:3.36,id:UT22084-001-002-627}}}“Upāli, it has been received and should not be received again.”
{{milestone:{label:3,id:UT22084-001-002-section-3-7}}}Rouse the Intention for the Restoration Rite
{{milestone:{label:3.37,id:UT22084-001-002-629}}}The venerable Upāli asked the Blessed Buddha, “Honorable One, what should a monk who is alone at a site do on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite?” 
{{milestone:{label:3.38,id:UT22084-001-002-630}}}“Upāli, that monk should sprinkle the monastery hall with water, sweep it, spread a fresh paste of dung, set up a lion throne, set out a seat, light a votive lamp, and give the opportunity for the Dharma to be heard.{{note:{index:192,id:UT22084-001-002-631}}} Later, he should sit in the highest place around and look in the four directions. If pure, like-minded monks should come, he should say, ‘O venerable ones! Come quickly! It is the fifteenth and the saṅgha’s restoration rite.’ 
{{milestone:{label:3.39,id:UT22084-001-002-632}}}“They should then sit together and perform the restoration rite. If they do so, all is well. If they do not, that monk should sit on his seat and say, ‘Today, the fifteenth, is the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, the monk named so-and-so. I therefore profess that I, the monk named so-and-so, am pure of hindering qualities. I ask that the gods accept my profession of purity. So that I, the monk named so-and-so, may perfect the body of pure conduct, today I sanction the restoration rite.’{{note:{index:193,id:UT22084-001-002-633}}}
{{milestone:{label:3.40,id:UT22084-001-002-634}}}“He should rouse the following intention and recite the words, ‘When I find a saṅgha assembly, I will participate in the full restoration rite together with the saṅgha and listen to the reciter recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra.’ Repeat these words verbatim a second and third time. 
{{milestone:{label:3.41,id:UT22084-001-002-635}}}“Where two monks are staying together, they should recite the words just given to one another. Likewise, where three monks are staying together, they should say them one by one in turn to one another. Where four monks are staying together, they should make a motion and then perform the restoration rite. In such a place, a sick monastic’s profession of purity should not be received. Where five or more monks are staying together, they should make a motion and then perform the restoration rite. In such a place, a sick monastic’s profession of purity may also be received. {{page:{number:43,id:UT22084-001-002-1886,folio:F.152.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:4,id:UT22084-001-002-section-4}}}The King
{{milestone:{label:4.1,id:UT22084-001-002-637}}}A summary:
{{milestone:{label:4.2,id:UT22084-001-002-638}}}The king apprehends a monk,
There is business so do not rise, 
Giving exemptions to the deranged,
And the ten recollections.
{{milestone:{label:4,id:UT22084-001-002-section-4-1}}}The King Apprehends a Monk
{{milestone:{label:4.3,id:UT22084-001-002-640}}}“If a king, bandit, murderer, brigand, or enemy apprehends a monk on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the monks should, on behalf of that monk, either go in person or send a messenger to say, ‘As this monk is our fellow brahmacārin, we ask that you release him.’ If he is released, then all is well. If he is not released, a second messenger should be sent to say, ‘As we have some business with this monk, we ask that you please release him.’ If he is released, then all is well. If he is not released, the monks should proceed to an inner circle and perform the restoration rite there.{{note:{index:194,id:UT22084-001-002-641}}} Then, the following day, they should endeavor to secure the monk’s freedom. If they so endeavor, then all is well. They will be guilty of a breach if they do not.”
{{milestone:{label:4,id:UT22084-001-002-section-4-2}}}There Is Business So Do Not Rise
{{milestone:{label:4.4,id:UT22084-001-002-643}}}Later, on the fifteenth, the Blessed One sat down on a seat placed before the saṅgha of monks and performed the restoration rite by reciting the saṅgha’s Prātimokṣa. The Blessed One then said to the monks, “There is some saṅgha business to attend to so please do not rise for a time.”
{{milestone:{label:4.5,id:UT22084-001-002-644}}}One monk then stood up from his seat, took his upper robe from one shoulder, turned to the Blessed One and, after bowing with palms pressed together, asked the Blessed One, “Honorable One, what should we do if the profession of purity made by a monk who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness at a site is received?”
{{milestone:{label:4.6,id:UT22084-001-002-645}}}The Blessed One replied, “That monk should receive the consent of the monk who, because he is pure, has offered his profession of purity.’ ”{{note:{index:195,id:UT22084-001-002-646}}}{{page:{number:44,id:UT22084-001-002-1887,folio:F.152.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:4.7,id:UT22084-001-002-647}}}Though the Blessed One told them to receive consent, the monks did not know how to do so, so the Blessed One said, “It may be received from one to one, one to two, or to a great many, so long as every monk in the saṅgha can be named. Monks, I will establish the rules of customary conduct by which a monk offers his consent. The monk offering his consent should take his upper robe from one shoulder, take off both sandals, and prostrate to the assembled in order of seniority before squatting with palms pressed together and saying, ‘Venerable ones, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, a monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness. I therefore profess that I, a monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness, am pure of hindering qualities. I offer my consent for the saṅgha to properly perform its duties.{{note:{index:196,id:UT22084-001-002-649}}} My restoration rite is pure, I give my consent and profess my purity. Let my profession be known.’
{{milestone:{label:4.8,id:UT22084-001-002-650}}}“Repeat that verbatim a second and third time. If the monk offering his consent physically communicates his consent, his consent should be announced. If the monk offering his consent verbally communicates his consent, his consent should be announced. If the monk offering his consent both physically and verbally communicates his consent, his consent should be announced. 
{{milestone:{label:4.9,id:UT22084-001-002-651}}}“If he neither physically nor verbally communicates his consent, the entire saṅgha should go to him or the monk should be brought among the saṅgha. They will be guilty of a breach if the entire saṅgha does not go to him, {{page:{number:45,id:UT22084-001-002-1888,folio:F.153.a}}} or if there is lack of a quorum due to his not being accepted among the saṅgha. They will be guilty of a breach if the monk offering his consent follows the rules of customary conduct but his consent is not accepted after being properly received.
{{milestone:{label:4.10,id:UT22084-001-002-653}}}“Monks, I will establish the rules of customary conduct for monks who receive consent. After he has received consent, the monk who has received consent should not run, nor should he rush, jump, jump over partitions, jump over ditches, jump onto verandas, sit in the sky above, go beyond the boundary, climb a ladder two rungs at a time, climb a staircase two steps at a time, spill over onto a causeway, fall asleep, or sit in equipoise. To fall asleep or to sit in equipoise are censured for two reasons: because one suggests disrespect and the other absentmindedness.
{{milestone:{label:4.11,id:UT22084-001-002-654}}}“Then, when the saṅgha elder says, ‘Announce the consent and professions of purity of those venerable ones who have not come. Let this profession be known,’ the monk who has received the consent sits before the monk seated in front and says, ‘Venerable, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite, for the monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness, at such and such a place, who is pure of hindering qualities. He has offered his consent for the saṅgha to properly perform its duties. His restoration rite is also pure, I announce his consent and profession of purity. {{page:{number:46,id:UT22084-001-002-1889,folio:F.153.b}}} Let this announcement be known.’
{{milestone:{label:4.12,id:UT22084-001-002-655}}}“Repeat this verbatim a second and third time. 
{{milestone:{label:4.13,id:UT22084-001-002-656}}}“Alternatively, the monk who has received consent should stand at the end of the line of seniority in the middle of the saṅgha and say, ‘Venerable saṅgha, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite, for the monk named so-and-so, who is sick, suffering, and tormented by illness, at such and such a place, who is pure of hindering qualities. He has offered his consent for the saṅgha to properly perform its duties. His restoration rite is also pure, I announce his consent and profession of purity. Let this announcement be known.’
{{milestone:{label:4.14,id:UT22084-001-002-657}}}“They will be guilty of a breach if the monk who has received the consent follows the rules of customary conduct but his announcement is not accepted after being properly received.” 
{{milestone:{label:4.15,id:UT22084-001-002-659}}}The venerable Upāli asked the Blessed Buddha, “Honorable One, if the monk receiving consent and a profession of purity comes to an end and dies immediately after having received consent and a profession of purity, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:4.16,id:UT22084-001-002-660}}}“Upāli, it has not been received and should be received again.”
{{milestone:{label:4.17,id:UT22084-001-002-661}}}“Honorable One, if the monk receiving consent and a profession of purity{{note:{index:197,id:UT22084-001-002-6611}}} makes an oath consenting to and professing to being a householder, or makes an oath that he is a novice, a person who has undergone castration, a person labeled a paṇḍaka, someone who has violated a nun, a matricide, a patricide, someone who has killed an arhat, someone who has caused a schism in the saṅgha, someone who has maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, a tīrthika, a convert to a tīrthika order, someone living under false pretenses, someone outside the common living, or someone denied the common living, has the profession of purity been received or not?” {{page:{number:47,id:UT22084-001-002-1890,folio:F.154.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:4.18,id:UT22084-001-002-662}}}“Upāli, it has not been received and should be received again.”
{{milestone:{label:4.19,id:UT22084-001-002-663}}}“Honorable One, if the monk receiving consent and a profession of purity comes to an end and dies afterwards while on his way, should the consent and profession of purity be declared received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:4.20,id:UT22084-001-002-664}}} “Upāli, they have not been received and should be received again.
{{milestone:{label:4.21,id:UT22084-001-002-665}}}“If the monk receiving consent and a profession of purity makes an oath consenting to and professing to being a householder, or makes an oath that he is a novice, a person who has undergone castration, a person labeled a paṇḍaka, someone who has violated a nun, a matricide, a patricide, someone who has killed an arhat, someone who has caused a schism in the saṅgha, someone who has maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, a tīrthika, a convert to a tīrthika order, someone living under false pretenses, someone outside the common living, or someone denied the common living, has the profession of purity been received or not?” 
{{milestone:{label:4.22,id:UT22084-001-002-666}}}“Upāli, they have not been received and should be received again.”
{{milestone:{label:4.23,id:UT22084-001-002-667}}}“If the monk receiving consent and a profession of purity comes to an end and dies while among the saṅgha after he has received consent and a profession of purity, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:4.24,id:UT22084-001-002-668}}}“Upāli, they have been received and should not be received again.” 
{{milestone:{label:4.25,id:UT22084-001-002-669}}}“If the monk receiving consent and a profession of purity makes an oath consenting to and professing to being a householder, or makes an oath that he is a novice, a person who has undergone castration, a person labeled a paṇḍaka, someone who has violated a nun, a matricide, a patricide, someone who has killed an arhat, someone who has caused a schism in the saṅgha, someone who has maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, a tīrthika, a convert to a tīrthika order, a person living under false pretenses, {{page:{number:48,id:UT22084-001-002-1891,folio:F.154.b}}} someone who is outside the common living, or someone who is denied the common living, has the profession of purity been received or not?”
{{milestone:{label:4.26,id:UT22084-001-002-670}}}“Upāli, they have been received and should not be received again.”
{{milestone:{label:4.27,id:UT22084-001-002-672}}}The venerable Upāli asked the Blessed Buddha, “Honorable One, what should a monk who is alone at a site do on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite?” 
{{milestone:{label:4.28,id:UT22084-001-002-673}}}“Upāli, that monk should sprinkle the floor of the monastery with water, sweep it, spread a fresh paste of dung over it, set up a lion throne, set out a seat, light a votive lamp, and give an opportunity for the Dharma to be heard. After that, he should sit in the highest place around and look into the four directions. If pure, like-minded monks should come, he should say, ‘O venerable ones! Come quickly! It is the fifteenth and the saṅgha’s restoration rite.’ 
{{milestone:{label:4.29,id:UT22084-001-002-674}}}“They should then sit together and perform the restoration rite. If they do so, all is well. If they do not, that monk should sit on his seat and say, ‘Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, the monk named so-and-so. I therefore profess that I, the monk named so-and-so, am pure of hindering qualities. I ask that the gods accept my profession of purity. So that I, the monk named so-and-so, may perfect the body of pure conduct, today I sanction the restoration rite.’
{{milestone:{label:4.30,id:UT22084-001-002-675}}}“He should rouse the following intention and recite the words, ‘When I find a saṅgha assembly, I will participate in the full restoration rite together with the saṅgha and listen to the reciter recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra.’ That should be repeated verbatim a second and third time. 
{{milestone:{label:4.31,id:UT22084-001-002-676}}}“Where two monks are staying together, they should recite the words just given to one another. Likewise, where three monks are staying together, {{page:{number:49,id:UT22084-001-002-1892,folio:F.155.a}}} they should say them one by one in turn to one another. Where four monks are staying together, they should make a motion and then perform the restoration rite. In such a place, a sick monastic’s consent and profession of purity should not be received. Where five or more monks are staying together, they should make a motion and then perform the restoration rite. In such a place, a sick monastic’s consent and profession of purity can also be received.
{{milestone:{label:4,id:UT22084-001-002-section-4-3}}}Giving Exemptions to the Deranged
{{milestone:{label:4.32,id:UT22084-001-002-678}}}The Blessed Buddha was staying at Prince Jeta’s Grove, Anāthapiṇḍada’s park, near Śrāvastī when the venerable Saikata, deranged, his mind disturbed, wandered around naked, sometimes coming to the saṅgha’s restoration rite site and sometimes not. Sometimes he participated with the saṅgha in the restoration rite, and sometimes he did not. Sometimes he attended the saṅgha’s special events and acts, and sometimes he did not. Sometimes he participated with the saṅgha in the saṅgha’s special events and acts, and sometimes he did not. Thus, when the monks found themselves unable to carry out certain acts due to their not having a quorum, they appealed to the Blessed One and the Blessed One replied, “Monks, an exemption for reasons of derangement should be given to the monk Saikata and others like him. It should be given in the following way. After seats have been arranged, strike the gaṇḍī beam and inform the monks of the matter at hand. Once the whole saṅgha is seated and has a quorum, one monk should make a motion and perform the act as follows:
{{milestone:{label:4.33,id:UT22084-001-002-679}}}“ ‘Venerable saṅgha, please listen. The monk Saikata,{{note:{index:198,id:UT22084-001-002-680}}} deranged, his mind disturbed, wanders around naked, sometimes coming to the saṅgha’s restoration rite site and sometimes not. {{page:{number:50,id:UT22084-001-002-1893,folio:F.155.b}}} Sometimes he participates with the saṅgha in the restoration rite and sometimes he does not. Sometimes he attends the saṅgha’s special events and acts and sometimes he does not. Sometimes he participates with the saṅgha in the saṅgha’s special events and acts and sometimes he does not. Thus, we monks find ourselves unable to carry out certain acts due to our, the monks, not having a quorum. Therefore, if the time is right and the saṅgha can accept it, I ask that the saṅgha grant an exemption. I ask that the saṅgha grant the monk Saikata an exemption for reasons of derangement. If he comes, do not attempt to stop him. If he goes, do not attempt to stop him. Whether the monk Saikata comes or goes, the saṅgha should not be deemed in discord when they perform the saṅgha’s restoration rite, lifting of restrictions, motions, acts by motion and resolution, or acts by motion and triple resolution.’
{{milestone:{label:4.34,id:UT22084-001-002-681}}}“That is the motion. The act is performed in the following way: 
{{milestone:{label:4.35,id:UT22084-001-002-682}}}“ ‘Venerable saṅgha, please listen. The monk Saikata, deranged, his mind disturbed, wanders around naked, sometimes coming to the saṅgha’s restoration rite site and sometimes not. Sometimes he participates with the saṅgha in the restoration rite, and sometimes he does not. Sometimes he attends the saṅgha’s special events and acts, and sometimes he does not. Sometimes he participates with the saṅgha in the saṅgha’s special events and acts, and sometimes he does not. Thus, we monks find ourselves unable to carry out certain acts due to not having a quorum. I ask that the saṅgha grant the monk Saikata an exemption for reasons of derangement. If he comes, do not attempt to stop him. If he goes, {{page:{number:51,id:UT22084-001-002-1894,folio:F.156.a}}} do not attempt to stop him. If he walks away, do not attempt to stop him. I ask those venerable ones who can accept our deeming the saṅgha should not be deemed in discord whether the monk Saikata comes or goes when they perform the saṅgha’s restoration rite, lifting of restrictions, motions, acts by motion and resolution, and acts by motion and triple resolution to remain silent. I ask those who cannot so accept it to speak now.’
{{milestone:{label:4.36,id:UT22084-001-002-683}}}“By expressing their acceptance and giving their consent, the saṅgha grants the monk Saikata an exemption by reason of derangement. By remaining silent, they assent to that.”
{{milestone:{label:4,id:UT22084-001-002-section-4-4}}}The Ten Recollections
{{milestone:{label:4.37,id:UT22084-001-002-685}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk recalls an offense, that monk should properly make amends for the offense before another monk as follows: he should take his upper robe from one shoulder, take off both sandals, and prostrate to the assembled in order of seniority before squatting with palms pressed together. While squatting before the monk with palms pressed together and head bowed, he should say, ‘Venerable, please listen. I, the monk named so-and-so, have incurred this offense. I, the monk named so-and-so, confess and disclose each and every one of those offenses before you, venerable; I do not conceal them. If I confess and disclose them, I will be at ease. If I do not confess and disclose them, I will not be at ease.’
{{milestone:{label:4.38,id:UT22084-001-002-686}}}“That should be repeated verbatim a second and third time. 
{{milestone:{label:4.39,id:UT22084-001-002-687}}}“He is then asked, ‘Do you recognize the offense?’
{{milestone:{label:4.40,id:UT22084-001-002-688}}}“The monk should reply, ‘I do.’
{{milestone:{label:4.41,id:UT22084-001-002-689}}}“He is then asked, ‘From now on, will you refrain from it?’
{{milestone:{label:4.42,id:UT22084-001-002-690}}}“He replies, ‘I will.’ 
{{milestone:{label:4.43,id:UT22084-001-002-691}}}“That should be repeated verbatim a second and third time.
{{milestone:{label:4.44,id:UT22084-001-002-692}}}“The confessor{{note:{index:199,id:UT22084-001-002-693}}} should then say, ‘That is the means.’
{{milestone:{label:4.45,id:UT22084-001-002-694}}}“The confessant{{note:{index:200,id:UT22084-001-002-695}}} should then reply, ‘Excellent.’
{{milestone:{label:4.46,id:UT22084-001-002-696}}}“After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this to be a hindrance to the restoration rite.{{note:{index:201,id:UT22084-001-002-697}}}{{page:{number:52,id:UT22084-001-002-1895,folio:F.156.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:4.47,id:UT22084-001-002-699}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk is already suspected of or uncertain{{note:{index:202,id:UT22084-001-002-700}}} about an offense, he should ask an upholder of the sūtras, the vinaya, or the mātṛkā about it. Once the suspicions and uncertainties regarding the offense have been resolved, he should properly make amends for the offense before another monk. After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.48,id:UT22084-001-002-702}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk recalls an offense while among the saṅgha, he should sanction{{note:{index:203,id:UT22084-001-002-703}}} that offense before another monk by saying, ‘Venerable, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, the monk so-and-so. I, the monk so-and-so, have recalled this and that offense while among the saṅgha. I, the monk so-and-so, sanction this offense in your presence so that I may perform the restoration rite today. I resolve that tomorrow morning I will properly make amends for{{note:{index:204,id:UT22084-001-002-704}}} that offense.’ After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.49,id:UT22084-001-002-706}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk is suspected of or becomes uncertain about an offense while among the saṅgha, he should go before another monk and sanction that offense by saying, ‘Venerable, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, the monk so-and-so. While among the saṅgha, I, the monk so-and-so, have become uncertain about this and that offense. I, the monk so-and-so, sanction this offense in your presence so that I may perform the restoration rite today. Tomorrow morning I will ask an upholder of the sūtras, the vinaya, or the mātṛkā about it and once my doubts and uncertainties regarding the offense have been clarified, {{page:{number:53,id:UT22084-001-002-1896,folio:F.157.a}}} I will properly make amends for the offense.’ After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.50,id:UT22084-001-002-708}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the monk reciter of The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recalls an offense while among the saṅgha, that monk should mentally sanction the offense by thinking, ‘Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, the monk so-and-so reciter of The Prātimokṣa Sūtra. I, the monk so-and-so reciter of The Prātimokṣa Sūtra, have recalled this and that offense while among the saṅgha, so I, the monk so-and-so reciter of The Prātimokṣa Sūtra, mentally sanction that offense so that I may perform the restoration rite today. I resolve that tomorrow morning I will properly make amends for that offense.’ After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.51,id:UT22084-001-002-710}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the monk reciter of The Prātimokṣa Sūtra becomes suspected of or uncertain about an offense while among the saṅgha, that monk should mentally sanction that offense by thinking, ‘Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. It is also the fifteenth, the restoration rite for me, the monk so-and-so charged with reciting The Prātimokṣa Sūtra. I, the monk so-and-so charged with reciting The Prātimokṣa Sūtra, am suspected of and have become uncertain about this and that offense while among the saṅgha, so I, the monk so-and-so charged with reciting The Prātimokṣa Sūtra, mentally sanction that offense so that I may perform the restoration rite today. Tomorrow morning I will ask an upholder of the sūtras, the vinaya, or the mātṛkā about it and once the suspicions and uncertainties regarding the offense have been clarified, I will properly make amends for the offense in accord with the Vinaya.’{{note:{index:205,id:UT22084-001-002-711}}}{{page:{number:54,id:UT22084-001-002-1897,folio:F.157.b}}} After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.52,id:UT22084-001-002-713}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the entire saṅgha has incurred offenses, some among the monks in whose presence they may later properly make amends should willingly go to another site in order to make amends for the offense in front of a monk. 
{{milestone:{label:4.53,id:UT22084-001-002-714}}}If they can do so, all is well. If they cannot, those monks should perform an act of motion alone as follows:{{note:{index:206,id:UT22084-001-002-715}}}
{{milestone:{label:4.54,id:UT22084-001-002-716}}}“ ‘Venerable ones, please listen. Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. We, the entire saṅgha, have incurred offenses, and so we should properly make amends for our offenses. Yet there are no monks among us who will willingly go to another site to properly make amends for the offenses in the presence of a monk. Therefore, if the time is right and the saṅgha can accept it, we ask that the saṅgha give their consent. The saṅgha sanctions that offense so that we may perform the restoration rite today. Later, we will properly make amends for those offenses in the presence of a monk.’
{{milestone:{label:4.55,id:UT22084-001-002-717}}}“That is the motion. After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.56,id:UT22084-001-002-719}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the entire saṅgha is suspected of or becomes uncertain about an offense, some among the monks, having gone to another site where there is a monk in whose presence they may properly make amends for, should willing ask an upholder of the sūtras, the vinaya, or the mātṛkā about them and, once their suspicions and uncertainties about the offense have been clarified, they should properly make amends. If they can do so, all is well. If they cannot, those monks should perform an act of motion alone as follows:
{{milestone:{label:4.57,id:UT22084-001-002-720}}}“ ‘Venerable ones, please listen. {{page:{number:55,id:UT22084-001-002-1898,folio:F.158.a}}} Today is the fifteenth, the saṅgha’s restoration rite. We, the entire saṅgha, are suspected of or have become uncertain, yet no monks among us, we who must confess, will willingly go to another site, where they might properly make amends for the offenses after clarifying our doubts and uncertainties regarding the offenses through asking an upholder of the sūtras, the vinaya, or the mātṛkā about them. Therefore, if the time is right and the saṅgha can accept it, we ask that the saṅgha give their consent. The saṅgha sanctions those offenses today so that we may perform the restoration rite. Later, we will ask an upholder of the sūtras, the vinaya, or the mātṛkā about them and once our doubts and uncertainties regarding them have been clarified, we will properly make amends for the offenses.’
{{milestone:{label:4.58,id:UT22084-001-002-721}}}“That is the motion. After that, the restoration rite should be performed. Monks, that is how the restoration rite should be performed; I do not declare this a hindrance to the restoration rite.
{{milestone:{label:4.59,id:UT22084-001-002-722}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the entire saṅgha except one resident monk have incurred offenses, they should say, in the presence of that monk—an acquaintance, a friend, an intimate, or a companion{{note:{index:207,id:UT22084-001-002-723}}}—‘Venerable, what comes of doing this or that?’ 
{{milestone:{label:4.60,id:UT22084-001-002-724}}}“ ‘An offense is incurred.’
{{milestone:{label:4.61,id:UT22084-001-002-725}}}“ ‘Well then, venerable, I too have done this or that.’ 
{{milestone:{label:4.62,id:UT22084-001-002-726}}}“ ‘Well then, venerable, you have incurred an offense.’
{{milestone:{label:4.63,id:UT22084-001-002-727}}}“ ‘Venerable, that is the case for the entire saṅgha, apart from you alone.’
{{milestone:{label:4.64,id:UT22084-001-002-728}}}“ ‘Then listen. You, venerable, should first make amends for your own offense. Then the entire saṅgha should ask you, “What comes of doing this or that?” ’{{note:{index:208,id:UT22084-001-002-729}}}
{{milestone:{label:4.65,id:UT22084-001-002-730}}} “If he will confess, the confessor should make the confessant confess in a place where the other monks might see and so confess too.{{note:{index:209,id:UT22084-001-002-731}}} If that is done, all is well. {{page:{number:56,id:UT22084-001-002-1899,folio:F.158.b}}} If it is not done, the confessor should not prompt the confessant against his will.{{note:{index:210,id:UT22084-001-002-732}}} He should not remind him against his will.{{note:{index:211,id:UT22084-001-002-733}}} He will be guilty of a breach if he prompts or reminds him against his will.
{{milestone:{label:4.66,id:UT22084-001-002-735}}}“If, on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, the entire saṅgha except one visiting monk have incurred offenses, they should say, in the presence of that monk—an acquaintance, a friend, an intimate, or a companion—‘Venerable, what comes of doing this or that?’
{{milestone:{label:4.67,id:UT22084-001-002-736}}}“ ‘An offense is incurred.’
{{milestone:{label:4.68,id:UT22084-001-002-737}}}“ ‘Well then, venerable, I too have done this or that.’
{{milestone:{label:4.69,id:UT22084-001-002-738}}}“ ‘Well then, venerable, you have incurred an offense.’
{{milestone:{label:4.70,id:UT22084-001-002-739}}}“ ‘Venerable, that is the case for the entire saṅgha, apart from you alone.’
{{milestone:{label:4.71,id:UT22084-001-002-740}}}“ ‘Then listen. You, venerable, should first make amends for your own offense. Then the entire saṅgha should ask you, “What comes of doing this or that?” ’
{{milestone:{label:4.72,id:UT22084-001-002-741}}} “If he will confess, the confessor should make the confessant confess in a place where the other monks might see and so confess too. If that is done, all is well. If it is not done, the confessor should not prompt the confessant against his will. He should not remind him against his will. He will be guilty of a breach if he prompts or reminds him against his will.”
{{milestone:{label:5,id:UT22084-001-002-section-5}}}Several Repetitions
{{milestone:{label:5.1,id:UT22084-001-002-743}}}A summary:
{{milestone:{label:5.2,id:UT22084-001-002-744}}}Several repetitions:{{note:{index:212,id:UT22084-001-002-745}}}lack of a quorum,
Numbers, going, and
The restoration rite of professed purity.
{{milestone:{label:5,id:UT22084-001-002-section-5-1}}}Lack of a Quorum
{{milestone:{label:5.3,id:UT22084-001-002-747}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’{{note:{index:213,id:UT22084-001-002-748}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.4,id:UT22084-001-002-749}}}“If those monks, with fabricated aims{{note:{index:214,id:UT22084-001-002-750}}} and fabricated preparations,{{note:{index:215,id:UT22084-001-002-751}}}{{page:{number:57,id:UT22084-001-002-1900,folio:F.159.a}}} make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a smaller number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.{{note:{index:216,id:UT22084-001-002-752}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.5,id:UT22084-001-002-754}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, is it valid or not for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived?’ 
{{milestone:{label:5.6,id:UT22084-001-002-755}}}“If those monks, with unsure aims and unsure preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a smaller number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a breach because of their unsure attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.7,id:UT22084-001-002-757}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, let those monks who have not yet arrived be absent, let them stay where they are, let them be separate, let them be far away.’
{{milestone:{label:5.8,id:UT22084-001-002-758}}}“If those monks, with divisive aims and divisive preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a smaller number of resident monks arrive later, {{page:{number:58,id:UT22084-001-002-1901,folio:F.159.b}}} they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a grievous fault because of their divisive attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.9,id:UT22084-001-002-760}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’ 
{{milestone:{label:5.10,id:UT22084-001-002-761}}}“If those monks, with fabricated aims and fabricated preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and an equal number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.11,id:UT22084-001-002-763}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, is it valid or not for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived?’ 
{{milestone:{label:5.12,id:UT22084-001-002-764}}}“If those monks, with unsure aims and unsure preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and an equal number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a breach because of their unsure attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.13,id:UT22084-001-002-766}}}“When four or more resident monks {{page:{number:59,id:UT22084-001-002-1902,folio:F.160.a}}} are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, let those monks who have not yet arrived be absent, let them stay where they are, let them be separate, let them be far away.’
{{milestone:{label:5.14,id:UT22084-001-002-767}}}“If those monks, with divisive aims and divisive preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and an equal number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a grievous fault because of their divisive attempts.

{{milestone:{label:5.16,id:UT22084-001-002-770}}}“If those monks, with fabricated aims and fabricated preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a greater number of resident monks arrive arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. The earlier group of monks will be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.

{{milestone:{label:5.165,id:UT22084-001-002-1001}}}An intervening summary:
{{milestone:{label:5.166,id:UT22084-001-002-1002}}}Fabricated, unsure, and divisiveness.{{note:{index:228,id:UT22084-001-002-1003}}}
{{milestone:{label:5,id:UT22084-001-002-section-5-2}}}Numbers
{{milestone:{label:5.167,id:UT22084-001-002-1005}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might not think, ‘There are monks who have not yet arrived,’ but instead, thinking of their duty and thinking there was a quorum,{{note:{index:229,id:UT22084-001-002-1006}}} they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation.{{note:{index:230,id:UT22084-001-002-1007}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.168,id:UT22084-001-002-1008}}}“If later a smaller number of resident monks arrives, the second group, once they have sat down in order of seniority, should perform the restoration rite and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation together with the first, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.169,id:UT22084-001-002-1010}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might not think, ‘There are monks who have not yet arrived,’ but instead, {{page:{number:93,id:UT22084-001-002-1936,folio:F.177.a}}} thinking of their duty and thinking there was a quorum, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation until the saṅgha has finished performing The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and the restoration rite. 
{{milestone:{label:5.170,id:UT22084-001-002-1011}}}“If, after that, a smaller number of resident monks arrives before the assembly rises and the monks depart,{{note:{index:231,id:UT22084-001-002-1012}}} the first group{{note:{index:232,id:UT22084-001-002-1013}}} should again, for the sake of the second, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.171,id:UT22084-001-002-1015}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might not think, ‘There are monks who have not yet arrived,’ but instead, thinking of their duty and thinking there was a quorum, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation until the saṅgha has finished performing The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and the restoration rite. 
{{milestone:{label:5.172,id:UT22084-001-002-1016}}}“If, after that, a smaller number of resident monks arrives after the assembly has risen and some monks have departed but while other monks are still there, they should gather the assembly if possible{{note:{index:233,id:UT22084-001-002-1017}}} and again, for the sake of the second, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. If they cannot gather the assembly, the later arrivals{{note:{index:234,id:UT22084-001-002-1018}}} should go to the inner circle, where they should perform the restoration rite and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.

{{milestone:{label:5.291,id:UT22084-001-002-1204}}}“When four or more visiting and resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might not think, ‘There are monks who have not yet arrived,’ but instead, thinking of their duty and thinking there was a quorum, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation until the saṅgha has finished performing The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and the restoration rite. 
{{milestone:{label:5.292,id:UT22084-001-002-1205}}}“If, after that, an equal number of resident monks arrives after the assembly has risen and some monks have departed but while other monks are still there, they should gather the assembly if possible and again, for the sake of the second, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. If they cannot gather the assembly, the later arrivals should go to the inner circle, where they should perform the restoration rite and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.293,id:UT22084-001-002-1207}}}“When four or more visiting and resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might not think, ‘There are monks who have not yet arrived,’ but instead, thinking of their duty and thinking there was a quorum, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation until the saṅgha has finished performing The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and the restoration rite.

{{milestone:{label:5.358,id:UT22084-001-002-1310}}}“If, after that, a greater number of visiting and resident monks arrives after the assembly has risen and some monks have departed but while other monks are still there, they should gather the assembly if possible and again, for the sake of the second, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation. {{milestone:{label:5.385,id:UT22084-001-002-1353}}}An intervening summary:
{{milestone:{label:5.386,id:UT22084-001-002-1354}}}Motion, have not yet departed, 
Some have departed, and all have departed. 
{{milestone:{label:5,id:UT22084-001-002-section-5-4}}}The Restoration Rite of Professed Purity
{{milestone:{label:5.387,id:UT22084-001-002-1356}}}“If it is the fifteenth according to the resident monks but the fourteenth or first{{note:{index:252,id:UT22084-001-002-1357}}} according to a smaller number of visiting monks, the visitors should defer to the greater number of residents.{{note:{index:253,id:UT22084-001-002-1358}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.388,id:UT22084-001-002-1359}}}“If it is the fifteenth according to the resident monks but the fourteenth or first according to an equal number of visiting monks, the visitors should defer to the equal number of residents.{{note:{index:254,id:UT22084-001-002-1360}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.389,id:UT22084-001-002-1361}}}“If it is the fifteenth according to a smaller group of resident monks but the fourteenth or first according to a greater number of visiting monks, the residents should defer to the greater number of visitors. 
{{milestone:{label:5.390,id:UT22084-001-002-1362}}}“If it is the fifteenth according to the visiting monks but the fourteenth or first according to a smaller number of resident monks, {{page:{number:137,id:UT22084-001-002-1980,folio:F.199.a}}} the residents should defer to the greater number of visitors. 
{{milestone:{label:5.391,id:UT22084-001-002-1363}}}“If it is the fifteenth according to the visiting monks but the fourteenth or first according to an equal number of resident monks, the visitors should defer to the equal number of residents.
{{milestone:{label:5.392,id:UT22084-001-002-1364}}} “If it is the fifteenth according to the visiting monks but the fourteenth or first according to a greater number of resident monks, the visitors should defer to the greater number of residents.”
{{milestone:{label:5.393,id:UT22084-001-002-1366}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might see evidence,{{note:{index:255,id:UT22084-001-002-1367}}} signs,{{note:{index:256,id:UT22084-001-002-1368}}} or marks{{note:{index:257,id:UT22084-001-002-1369}}} of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff,{{note:{index:258,id:UT22084-001-002-1370}}} cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, let those monks who have not yet arrived be absent, let them stay where they are, let them be separate, let them be far away.’{{note:{index:259,id:UT22084-001-002-1371}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.394,id:UT22084-001-002-1372}}}“If those monks, with divisive aims and divisive preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and later a smaller number of visiting monks arrives, the earlier group of monks should again make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a grievous fault because of their divisive attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.395,id:UT22084-001-002-1374}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, {{page:{number:138,id:UT22084-001-002-1981,folio:F.199.b}}} they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, is it valid or not for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived?’ 
{{milestone:{label:5.396,id:UT22084-001-002-1375}}}“If those monks, with unsure aims and unsure preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a smaller number of visiting monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their unsure attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.397,id:UT22084-001-002-1377}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.398,id:UT22084-001-002-1378}}}“If, heedless of duty and thinking of discord,{{note:{index:260,id:UT22084-001-002-1379}}}{{page:{number:139,id:UT22084-001-002-1982,folio:F.200.a}}} they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a smaller number of visiting monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their attempts at discord.
{{milestone:{label:5.399,id:UT22084-001-002-1381}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.400,id:UT22084-001-002-1382}}}“If those monks, with fabricated aims and fabricated preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a smaller number of visiting monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.401,id:UT22084-001-002-1384}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, {{page:{number:140,id:UT22084-001-002-1983,folio:F.200.b}}} water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.402,id:UT22084-001-002-1385}}}“If, having sincerely sought but not found any late arrivals, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and a smaller number of visiting monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.403,id:UT22084-001-002-1387}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.404,id:UT22084-001-002-1388}}}“If, having sincerely sought late arrivals, they find some, the earlier group should sit together with the later, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.405,id:UT22084-001-002-1390}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, {{page:{number:141,id:UT22084-001-002-1984,folio:F.201.a}}} they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, let those monks who have not yet arrived be absent, let them stay where they are, let them be separate, let them be far away.’{{note:{index:261,id:UT22084-001-002-1391}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.406,id:UT22084-001-002-1392}}}“If those monks, with divisive aims and divisive preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and later an equal number of visiting monks arrives, the earlier group of monks should again make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a grievous fault because of their divisive attempts.

{{milestone:{label:5.412,id:UT22084-001-002-1401}}}“If those monks, with fabricated aims and fabricated preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and an equal number of visiting monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.413,id:UT22084-001-002-1403}}}“When four or more resident monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might see evidence, signs, or marks of visiting monks such as another’s begging bowl, robe, staff, cushion, water jug, oil lamp, hat, laced boots, or sandals, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.414,id:UT22084-001-002-1404}}}“If, having sincerely sought but not found any late arrivals, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and an equal number of visiting monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.

{{milestone:{label:5.519,id:UT22084-001-002-1574}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.520,id:UT22084-001-002-1575}}}“If those monks, with fabricated aims and fabricated preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and an equal number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.521,id:UT22084-001-002-1577}}}“When four or more visiting monks {{page:{number:175,id:UT22084-001-002-2018,folio:F.218.a}}} are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.522,id:UT22084-001-002-1578}}}“If, having sincerely sought but not found any late arrivals, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and an equal number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.523,id:UT22084-001-002-1580}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.524,id:UT22084-001-002-1581}}}“If, having sincerely sought late arrivals, they find some, the earlier group should sit together with the later, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, {{page:{number:176,id:UT22084-001-002-2019,folio:F.218.b}}} in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach. 
{{milestone:{label:5.525,id:UT22084-001-002-1583}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, let those monks who have not yet arrived be absent, let them stay where they are, let them be separate, let them be far away.’{{note:{index:274,id:UT22084-001-002-1584}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.526,id:UT22084-001-002-1585}}}“If those monks, with divisive aims and divisive preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and later a greater number of resident monks arrives, the earlier group of monks should again make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a grievous fault because of their divisive attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.527,id:UT22084-001-002-1587}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, is it valid or not for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived?’ {{page:{number:177,id:UT22084-001-002-2020,folio:F.219.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.528,id:UT22084-001-002-1588}}}“If those monks, with unsure aims and unsure preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a greater number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their unsure attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.529,id:UT22084-001-002-1590}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.530,id:UT22084-001-002-1591}}}If, heedless of duty and thinking of discord, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a greater number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their attempts at discord.
{{milestone:{label:5.531,id:UT22084-001-002-1593}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might {{page:{number:178,id:UT22084-001-002-2021,folio:F.219.b}}} hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.532,id:UT22084-001-002-1594}}}If those monks, with fabricated aims and fabricated preparations, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, and a greater number of resident monks arrive later, they too should make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach because of their fabricated attempts.
{{milestone:{label:5.533,id:UT22084-001-002-1596}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.534,id:UT22084-001-002-1597}}}“If having sincerely sought but not found any late arrivals, they make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation and later a greater number of resident monks arrives, the earlier group of monks {{page:{number:179,id:UT22084-001-002-2022,folio:F.220.a}}} should again make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.
{{milestone:{label:5.535,id:UT22084-001-002-1599}}}“When four or more visiting monks are seated and have a quorum on the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, they might hear evidence, signs, or marks of resident monks such as the sound of residents’ staffs, the patter of feet, the clearing of throats, the rattle of locks and keys, and the tone of voices, and they might think, ‘If there are monks who have not yet arrived, it is not valid for us to make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation without those monks who have not yet arrived.’
{{milestone:{label:5.536,id:UT22084-001-002-1600}}}“If, having sincerely sought late arrivals, they find some, the earlier group should sit together with the later, make a motion, perform the restoration rite, and recite The Prātimokṣa Sūtra recitation, in which case the earlier group of monks will not be guilty of a breach.”
{{milestone:{label:5.537,id:UT22084-001-002-1601}}}An intervening summary:
{{milestone:{label:5.538,id:UT22084-001-002-1602}}}Divisiveness, unsure, discord,
Fabricated, not found, and finding. 
{{milestone:{label:5.539,id:UT22084-001-002-1604}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should leave a site with monks{{note:{index:275,id:UT22084-001-002-1605}}} and go to a site with monks where pure, like-minded monks have settled. 
{{milestone:{label:5.540,id:UT22084-001-002-1606}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should not leave a site with monks and go to a site with monks where the monks who have settled there argue, scold, fight, quarrel, or sow division, unless there are dangers{{note:{index:276,id:UT22084-001-002-1607}}} at the site where he is staying or the entire saṅgha is going there.
{{milestone:{label:5.541,id:UT22084-001-002-1609}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should leave a site with monks and go to a site with monks {{page:{number:180,id:UT22084-001-002-2023,folio:F.220.b}}} or a nonsite where pure, like-minded monks have settled.
{{milestone:{label:5.542,id:UT22084-001-002-1610}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should not leave a site with monks and go to a site or a nonsite with monks where the monks who have settled there argue, scold, fight, quarrel, or sow division, unless there are dangers at the site where he is staying or the entire saṅgha is going there.
{{milestone:{label:5.543,id:UT22084-001-002-1612}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should leave a site or a nonsite with monks and go to a site or a nonsite with monks where pure, like-minded monks have settled.
{{milestone:{label:5.544,id:UT22084-001-002-1613}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should not leave a site or a nonsite with monks and go to a site or a nonsite with monks where the monks who have settled there argue, scold, fight, quarrel, or sow division, unless there are dangers at the site where he is staying or the entire saṅgha is going there.
{{milestone:{label:5.545,id:UT22084-001-002-1615}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should leave a site with monks, a nonsite with monks, or a site/nonsite with monks and go to a site without monks where his body and mind will be at ease. 
{{milestone:{label:5.546,id:UT22084-001-002-1616}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should not leave a site with monks, a nonsite with monks, or a site/nonsite with monks and go to a site without monks, unless there are dangers at the site where he is staying or the entire saṅgha is going there.
{{milestone:{label:5.547,id:UT22084-001-002-1618}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should leave a site with monks, a nonsite with monks, {{page:{number:181,id:UT22084-001-002-2024,folio:F.221.a}}} or a site/nonsite with monks and go to a site without monks where his body and mind will be at ease. 
{{milestone:{label:5.548,id:UT22084-001-002-1619}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should not leave a site with monks, a nonsite with monks, a site/nonsite with monks, or a site without monks and go to a different site without monks unless there are dangers at the site where he is staying or the entire saṅgha is going there.
{{milestone:{label:5.549,id:UT22084-001-002-1621}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should leave a site with monks, a nonsite with monks, a site/nonsite with monks, a site without monks, or a nonsite without monks and go to a site/nonsite without monks where his body and mind will be at ease.{{note:{index:277,id:UT22084-001-002-1622}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.550,id:UT22084-001-002-1623}}}“On the fifteenth, the day of the restoration rite, a monk should not leave a site with monks, a nonsite with monks, a site/nonsite with monks, or a site/nonsite with or without monks and go to a site/nonsite without monks, unless there are dangers at the site where he is staying or the entire saṅgha is going there.
{{milestone:{label:5.551,id:UT22084-001-002-1624}}}“What is a ‘site with monks’? A site where all acts are witnessed.{{note:{index:278,id:UT22084-001-002-1625}}} What is a ‘nonsite with monks’? A site where no acts are witnessed. What is a ‘site/nonsite with monks’? A site where some acts are witnessed while other acts are not. What is a ‘site without monks’? A nuns’ site. What is a ‘nonsite without monks’? A tīrthikas’ site. What is a ‘site/nonsite without monks’? {{page:{number:182,id:UT22084-001-002-2025,folio:F.221.b}}} An uninhabited site. 
{{milestone:{label:5.552,id:UT22084-001-002-1626}}}“Monks should not perform the restoration rite, the lifting of restrictions, motions, acts by motion and resolution, or acts by motion and triple resolution in a place where householders are gathered or staying. 
{{milestone:{label:5.553,id:UT22084-001-002-1627}}}“Monks should not perform the restoration rite, the lifting of restrictions, motions, acts by motion and resolution, or acts by motion and triple resolution in a place where those unfit for the training—those who have not professed as ascetics,{{note:{index:279,id:UT22084-001-002-1628}}} those who have undergone castration, persons labeled a paṇḍaka, those who have violated a nun, patricides, matricides, those who have killed an arhat, those who have caused a schism in the saṅgha, those who have maliciously drawn blood from a tathāgata, tīrthikas, members of a tīrthika order, persons living under false pretenses, persons who are outside the common living, and persons who are denied the common living—are gathered or staying.
{{milestone:{label:5.554,id:UT22084-001-002-1629}}}“Monks will not be guilty of a breach if the restoration rite, the lifting of restrictions, motions, acts by motion and resolution, or acts by motion and triple resolution are performed in a place where all who have gathered and are staying are pure and like-minded.
{{milestone:{label:5.555,id:UT22084-001-002-1630}}} “They will be guilty of a breach if acts are performed without a quorum.” 
{{milestone:{label:5.556,id:UT22084-001-002-1631}}}This concludes “The Chapter on the Restoration Rite.”{{note:{index:280,id:UT22084-001-002-1632}}}
